25:T40a0,<entryFree id="n15180" key="رَدَّهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">رَدَّهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar" marker="rada3a">رَدَدَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, M, L,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَدٌّ</foreign> (S, M, Msb, K, &amp;c.) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَدٌّ</foreign> (S, M, L, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرْدُودٌ</foreign>, (S, L, K,) this last an inf. n. like <foreign lang="ar">مَحْلُوفٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَعْقُولٌ</foreign>, (S, L,) and <foreign lang="ar">رِدَّةٌ</foreign> (S [there said to be an inf. n., like <foreign lang="ar">رَدٌّ</foreign> of <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّهُ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="radu3a">رَدُدَ</orth>
                  </form>,]) and <foreign lang="ar">رِدِّيدَى</foreign>, (S, L, K, [but in the S and L merely said to be syn. with <foreign lang="ar">رَدٌّ</foreign>,]) an intensive form, (Mgh, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَرْدَادٌ</foreign>, which is [also] an intensive or a frequentative inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّهُ</foreign>, (Sb, M, L,) and likewise an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">ردّدهُ</foreign>; (Sb, S, M, L;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15180-1" target="ارتدّهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (M, L;) <hi rend="ital">He made,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">caused, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to return, go back, come back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">revert; sent, turned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">put, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">away; returned, rejected, repelled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">averted, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَهُ</foreign>, (S, M, L, Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">صَرَفَهُ</foreign>, (S, M, L, K) and <foreign lang="ar">دَفَعَهُ</foreign>; (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">دفع</foreign>, &amp;c.;) <foreign lang="ar">عَنْ وَجْهِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from his,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">its, course</hi>]. (S, M.) Hence, in the Kur [xxx. 42 and xlii. 46], <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمٌ لَا مَرَدَّ لَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A day which there shall be no repelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">averting</hi>], meaning the day of resurrection. (Th, M, L.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">أَمْرُ ٱللّٰهِ لَا مَرَدَّ لَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The command of God, there is no repelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">averting it.</hi> (L.) And <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ لِأَمْرِ ٱللّٰهِ مَرْدُودٌ</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">رَدٌّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is no repelling,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">averting, the command of God.</hi>] (A.) And <pb n="1062"/> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّهُ عَنِ الأَمْرِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made him to return</hi> or <hi rend="ital">revert,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">turned him back</hi> or <hi rend="ital">away, with gentleness, from the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">لَدَّهُ</foreign>. (T, L.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ</foreign> is made doubly trans. with <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى</foreign> to the second objective complement when honour is intended to be shown, and with <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى</foreign> when dishonour is intended; and they adduce as evidence of the correctness of their assertion the sayings in the Kur [xxviii. 12] <foreign lang="ar">فَرَدَدْنَاهُ إِلَى أُمِّهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">So we returned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">restored, him to his mother</hi>] and [iii. 142] <foreign lang="ar">يَرُدُّوكُمْ عَلَى أَعْقَابِكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They will turn you back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cause you to return, to your former condition</hi>]: but instances may be found at variance with this assertion. (MF.) [Such instances are of frequent occurrence; though in others, the distinction pointed out above is observed, as may be seen in what here follows.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّهُ إِلَى مَنْزِلِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He sent him back to his abode.</hi> (S, L, Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ إِلَيْهِ جَوَابًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He returned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rendered, to him a reply,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an answer;</hi> (S, A, * L, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">he sent to him a reply,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an answer.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He replied to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">answered him, in an absolute sense;</hi> (L;) and also, <hi rend="ital">by way of refutation</hi> or <hi rend="ital">objection,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">he replied against him;</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَقَالَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">and said,</hi> or <foreign lang="ar">بِقَوْلِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">by his saying.</hi> (TA &amp;c., passim.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He returned to him the salutation.</hi> (The Trads. &amp;c., passim.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ الوَدِيعَةَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He returned, rendered, restored,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sent</hi> [<hi rend="ital">back</hi>], <hi rend="ital">to him the deposite;</hi> (Msb;) and <foreign lang="ar">المَنِيحَةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the she-camel,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goat, lent to him for him to milk her</hi>]. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">منح</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ الشَّىْءَ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, L, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">رَدٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَدٌّ</foreign>, (Mgh,) <hi rend="ital">He rejected the thing,</hi> (such as a gift, A, and bad money, L,) <hi rend="ital">refusing to receive it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">accept it, from him;</hi> [<hi rend="ital">as though he cast it back at him;</hi>] and so <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n15180-2" target="رَادَّهُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>الشَّىْءَ</foreign>. (S, L, K. *) And in like manner, <hi rend="ital">He rejected the thing in reply to him, charging him with error in respect of it.</hi> (S, L, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَدْتُ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I rebutted, rejected,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">repudiated, in reply to him, his saying, charging him with error therein; I refused him my assent to it</hi>]. (A, Msb.) [And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَدْتُ قَوْلَهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I rebutted, rejected,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">repudiated, in reply,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">replication, his saying, as wrong,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">erroneous; refuted it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">refelled it; refused assent to it; controverted it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">contradicted it.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ الأَمْرَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He refused assent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">consent, to the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ عَلَيْهِ الأَمْرَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He refused him his assent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">consent, to the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ السَّائِلَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He turned back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">away, the beggar,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">asker, from the object of his want:</hi> (A:) [<hi rend="ital">he rebuffed him:</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">he sent away,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dismissed, the beggar,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">asker, either with refusal</hi> or <hi rend="ital">with a gift:</hi> occurring in trads. with both of these meanings. (L.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ البَابَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He shut,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">closed, the door.</hi> (Mgh. [See <foreign lang="ar">مَرْدُودٌ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">رَدَّ يَدَهُ إِلَى سَيْفِهِ</foreign> is a phrase of frequent occurrence, meaning <hi rend="ital">He put back his hand to his sword;</hi> it being hung behind him: (see 4 in art. <foreign lang="ar">خلف</foreign>:) and hence, simply, <hi rend="ital">he put his hand to his sword.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">فَرَدُّوا</foreign>
